O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	Oh, my very dear sons, I have completed for you this book which is the last of the science of medicine, along with its completion, and have made the end through its expositions and its declarations. 
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I complete it for you with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, that is to say "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is neglected in our region and is completely foreign, the science is lost and fragmented, and there remains nothing of it except the short descriptions in the books of the ancients which hands have copied.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this has come error and vanity, and understanding is obscured and knowledge is driven away.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	Now it seems to me that I want to revive it with the organization of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and I will include with it the forms of cautery irons, and of other instruments of the work with the addition of the description and preparation of them, as is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no good master of hands is found in our time, the art of medicine is diminished.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And whoever undertakes it must excel in the science of anatomy, as Galen said, so much that he knows the arrangement of the limbs, and their forms and connections and separations, and has knowledge of the bones and nerves and arms and their number, and the movement of the moving and resting veins, and the place of their origin.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And therefore Hippocrates said that the name with the name is much, and with the work is little; and especially in the art of the hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you in the introduction of this book that whoever is not knowledgeable about the things mentioned above, let him beware that he does not fall into error and that he does not kill people; so that I have often seen many of those who meddle in this science and thus abandon themselves without knowledge and without experience. 
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a foolish doctor who cut into a scrofulous abscess in the neck of a woman, and cut the arteries of the neck; so much blood came out that the woman fell dead in his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And I saw another doctor who extracted a stone from an elderly man, and the stone was large; he took with it a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called there to extract it, and I saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and I knew well that if he were cut he would die from it.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another doctor who took into his care a duke of our land who had a broken leg, and with the break there was a wound; and the doctor, full of ignorance, tightened the break over the wound with splints by strong binding, and left no opening at all for the wound, and left it like that for a while; and he ordered him not to untie it; and it remained like that until the leg was completely swollen and the foot as well, and it came to ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and I hastened to come and unbind the leg; and when I had unbound it, he was at peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But all the same the infection was already established in the limb, and I could not heal it; and the infection did not stop spreading through the limb until the limb was completely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another doctor who lanced a festering abscess, and then it became inflamed through the incompetence of his treatment.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a canker, when it is full of melancholic humor, should not be touched with iron unless it is in such a place that all that is corrupted can be removed.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And therefore, dear son, you need to know that manual work is divided into two parts: namely, work where there is danger in many forms; and I will show in each place of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	Therefore, it is necessary that you protect yourself, so that foolish doctors cannot speak ill of you. So take up your tools with reason, and treat your patients gently and firmly, and use the best method so that by the grace of God you achieve a successful outcome and are praised; and leave the dreadful diseases of difficult healing; and remove your tools from that which makes you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you can go from this world to the next with glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galen said in some of his admonishments: "Do not undertake to treat a bad disease, lest you be called a foolish doctor.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have divided this treatise into three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter is about fire cauteries and sharp medicinal cauteries, and the chapter is organized from the head down to the feet; and about the forms of the instruments, and the cautery irons, and everything that is necessary for the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and cupping glasses and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and the chapter is organized with the forms of the instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and sprains, and similar things; and it is organized from the head down to the feet, and with the forms of the instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Before we recall the work, it is necessary that I describe the quality of the help and the harm of each complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the qualities of help and harm are the longest discourse and subtle science and hidden secret; and many wise men have spoken of this, and agreed on it; and their words suffice little for me, for I fear the length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cautery helps universally every complexion where there is matter, except for two complexions: that is to say, a hot complexion without matter, and a dry complexion without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In a hot and dry complexion together with matter, some disagreed and said that cautery is a great help there; and others said the opposite: that cautery is not good for an illness that comes from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot, and a hot illness should not be treated by heat, nor by dryness; and he who said the opposite said that cautery is a great help for a hot and dry illness that comes into the body of men. 
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of a man and his moisture to the complexion of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement. 
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have sometimes found it by experiment.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And in any case, no one should interfere except those who have experience and who know, by long use, the chapter of cauteries, and the diversity of human complexions, and the dispositions and causes of their illnesses, and the occurrences and the length of time; we have no fear of other complexions, especially with cold and moist illnesses.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the physicians assembled and agreed on the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, son, that cautery with fire is among the secrets of cures, and of greater benefit than cautery with burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and does not go beyond the limb that is burned, and does not harm other limbs except a little.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Burning medicines spread from one limb to another, and cause illnesses in the limb that are difficult to heal; and perhaps kill the patient. Fire, because of its loftiness and the goodness of its substance, does not do this, unless there is excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And this I have found through experiment and the length of service and study that I have put into the art, and it was based on the truth of things; and therefore I excuse myself for the length of the speech, for I do not want to deprive you of the secret that lies in fire, and the quality of the work, how it expels illnesses from the body, as the philosopher says in demonstrating it; now receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agreed on what time cauterizations should be done, and they chose spring.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cautery is suitable in all seasons, because the sudden harm is lessened by the help of the cautery; and especially if the cautery is for necessary, sudden and urgent pains that cannot wait for the time when a greater malady might come to the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And do not ever think, dear son, as the foolish physicians do; for the illness that is healed by cautery does not return; and they say so; but it is not as they think, because cautery is nothing but a medicine that changes the complexion, and dries the humors that are the cause of the pain, and is worth more than medicine because of the speed of its effect, and because of the virtue of its work and its mastery.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And it is possible that the illness sometimes comes according to the complexion of the patient and the location of the illness and its nature; and superfluities are gathered in him by the acquisition of foods and similar things, unless cautery is administered in a place where there are few superfluities and moisture, such as cautery of teeth for pain, and similar things, and such pain does not return; but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cautery is called the last of medicines, and it is true; but they do not believe that cautery is useful after medicine, but their understanding is false, and cautery is the last of medicines because when we administer kinds of treatments for some illness and they are not effective, then we administer cautery, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Then it is clear that cautery is the last of medicines, not according to the understanding of the foolish physicians.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that cautery with a gold instrument is better than with iron, and they said this only because of the quality of gold and because of the excellence of its substance; and they said that the site of the cautery does not suppurate, but this is not true for I have tested it, and have found that it is true in some men; and gold cautery is better than iron, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And yet when you heat a gold instrument, you do not know when it is hot by the color of the gold, and it cools down quickly; and if it is heated too much, it melts in the fire; and thus there is considerable impediment.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason we use iron cautery because we have it better prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Now I have arranged this chapter from head to toe, so that the way is easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	Of the olive-shaped cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is good for moisture and coldness on the brain, and there are two that are made for a disease called "soda", and for many humors that descend from the head to the eyes, and to the ears, and for a multitude of dreams and toothache and sore throat, and especially for all diseases that come from coldness such as paralysis and lethargy and apoplexy and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The method for this cautery is that the patient be purged by a dissolving medicine cleansing the head for three or four nights, according to what the strength, age and constitution of the patient can bear; and then shave the patient's head.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	Then have him sit cross-legged between your hands, and place his hands on his chest; then place the base of your palm on the bridge of his nose between his two eyes; and where your middle finger falls, bleed from there, then heat the cautery which is called "olive-shaped", of which this is the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it on the spot marked with ink, and make it descend by pressing your hand little by little while turning it; then lift your hand quickly, and look at the place to see if you see the bone just a little; and if you do not see it, repeat the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you; then take a little salt, and put it in water and soak cotton in it, and place it on the spot, and leave it for three days; then put on cotton soaked in butter; and leave it on until the burn is gone; then treat the wound with the ointment called "tetrapharmakon", until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And the ancients said that the longer the wound remains open, the more it is purged; and for this it helps to change dressings.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And some of these said that one should leave the cautery until part of the bone is burned, and then cut away what is burned from the bone, and it should be treated.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And others say that one should leave the cautery on, and push so hard that one lowers the bone as wide as a whorl that women put on their spindles so that the humors come out more easily; and one should leave the wound open for a long time; then one should clean and solder it.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two ways of cauterizing do not seem to me to be good at all, except in some men where there is a way of fear; and it seems to me that I should leave it; for the head is weakened by the continuous solutions of nature, as we witness in other limbs; and even when the patient's head is naturally weak, the first type of cautery is safer and better for me, and this one I use in all work, with salvation.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the old headache
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When a chronic pain comes in the whole head, and lasts a long time, the patient should use irises and pills which are called "cochie", and purging of the head and oils and plasters; and if the cautery that we have spoken of before is done, and it is not effective.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care if the patient's head is of a strong nature, and that it is not too cold; then cauterize it a little under the cautery that we mentioned above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After that, make a cautery on each temple of the head down to the bone, as we have said before, and make a cautery in the place which is called "vessels"; and it is a place where one puts cupping glasses; and lighten your hand so that you do not go down to the bone: the patient feels much greater pain in this cautery than in the others, and I will speak of it elsewhere; and it is necessary that the cauteries of the temples be more subtle than those with which one cauterizes the middle of the head, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	of the cautery of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When a sudden pain comes in one part of the head, and the illness extends to the eye, and the head has been purged by cleansing medicines, and the other treatments that I mentioned in the division of illnesses have been done, and all this is not effective: then make cauteries for him in two ways, that is to say with a sharp medicine and with iron.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cautery with sharp medicine is that you take a clove of garlic, and remove the skin and cut it a little at both ends, and then split the temple where the pain is in such a way that you can put the clove of garlic under the skin; and when it is put in, bind it and tighten it well and leave it like that for twelve hours; and then untie it and pull out the clove of garlic, and leave the wound like that for two or three days; then put on cotton dipped in butter until pus comes out.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	Afterward treat it with ointment until it is healed; and if you wish, do this with some burning medicines that I have written about in the twelfth treatise on burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The cautery with iron is in this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery, of which this is the shape:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "closed" because the head is made in the shape of a nail where it has a little curvature, and in the middle has a small appearance; and place it on the painful spot, and hold your hand and turn the iron a little lightly, so that half the thickness of the skin is burned; and lift your hand so that the artery, which is outside, does not burn, and from which an abundance of blood flows.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	Afterward, put cotton in salt water, and place it on the spot for three days; then put cotton soaked in butter there, and then treat the area with ointment until it is healed; and if you want to cauterize this migraine with the cautery that is called "cultellar", use just the tip, and be careful not to cut the artery in this migraine which is not old.
de emigraine	of migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you treat a migraine as we have said before in the divisions of illnesses, and it is not effective, and you see that the aforementioned cauterizations with medicine and iron are not sufficient, then you must heat the cautery which is called "cultellar" until it is white; and first mark on the painful spot a line half a finger long, and remove your hand immediately, and restrain yourself so that you do not cut the artery and that you do not go down to the bone; and beware of the mandible which moves when one chews, and the nerve which controls it so that spasms do not occur in the patient, and beware of bleeding from the artery when it is cut, where cutting is very dangerous, especially for one who is not familiar with it, and who is not a student and experienced; and leaves the work half done; but I will tell you how to stop the blood when the artery is cut, and I will show you where it is appropriate in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that this cauterization is not sufficient for the illness, and the patient is suffering, cauterize him in the middle of the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it is healed; and if you wish, administer the cautery that we mentioned in the chapter on the extraction of the artery, with the cautery that has two blades; and this cautery is better than the other and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of ear pain from cold
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain from cold occurs in the ear, and one has applied dissolving medicines and other treatments that we have mentioned in the division, and the pain does not change, then heat this cautery which is called "point," of which here is the form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterward, prick all around the affected ear, or around both if the pain is in both, and stay a little above the base of the ear after you have marked the spot with ink; and make ten pricks around each ear; then treat the area until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	of the contortion/spasm of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Contortion/spasm that should be treated with cautery is only that which arises from phlegm, as we have said in the divisions of illness; and do not apply cautery to similar conditions that come from dryness and nerve spasm.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you treat this type of contortion/spasm that arises from phlegm with purges and head cleansings and gargles, and that is not effective, then you must cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one at the base of the ear, and another a little outside the temple, and the third at the joining of the two lips; and place the cautery on the part that appears healthy, and make the cautery next to the top of the ear a little below the crown of the head, and another on the temple as long as a thumb; and leave the cautery in place until half of the core is burned; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the appearance is like the small knife that we have described before, but it is a little more slender and the blade should be a little thicker; afterward treat the area as I have said before, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is chronic and you treat it as we have said, and it is not effective, and the patient does not have a fever, then make four cauteries: two on the two corners/temples of the head, and one in the middle of the head, and one in the place that is called "vessels" as we have said before, and the last cautery on the pit of the stomach; and it should be treated as we have said before.
de litargie	of lethargy
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this illness it is necessary to give the patient strong herbs and pills cleansing the brain; afterward shave the patient's entire head, and apply to the occiput a mustard plaster, which is described in the treatise on plasters; and this is the method of cauterization: apply it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If he is healed thus, good; and if not, then make three cauteries from the middle of the head descending down to the neck, and have a space between each cautery of one finger's width; and treat it like the others, and if you wish to add to it, and the patient is tolerant, make a cautery in the middle; and if necessary, two others on the two temples, and treat it until he is healed; and let the cautery be the one called "olive-shaped", as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	of coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary that the head be cleansed with herbs and with what we have said before; afterward shave the head of the patient, then make a cautery in the middle of the head and on each temple, and one behind and three on the spine of the neck; and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient is tolerant, and the illness is severe, make four cauteries on the spine of the back; and leave them until the core is mostly burned, and lift your hand; afterward treat it until he is healed, and let the cautery be the one called "olive-shaped" which we have mentioned before.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The epileptic should not use cautery except for the one who is phlegmatic, and it is necessary to first cleanse the brain with herbs and other treatments that we have mentioned in the section when the patient is strong and able to tolerate medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is a child who cannot tolerate it, make him gargle and chew things that cleanse the brain often with good foods; afterward shave the middle of his head, and make a cautery there according to what we have said before, and a cautery on the forehead, and on each temple; and if the patient is strong and tolerant, make cauteries as I have said for the one who has paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and the neck, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to the manner I have described.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is a child, make a subtle cautery in this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When because of melancholia the superfluities or the humors are corrupted and the phlegm is thick, then cauterize him with such cauteries as we have described for the one who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if because of melancholia the superfluity tends towards melancholia, and the body of the patient is moist, then give him to drink something by which the brain is cleansed, according to what is stated previously in the section.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterward shave the head of the patient; then make a well-made compress of linen, like a circle, and place it in the middle of the head; and let the patient be seated cross-legged, and be well held on all sides; then present the ointment, and aged sheep's butter is good; and warm it moderately over a fire, so that the finger, when placed in it, can bear it; then empty the circle inside the middle of the head, and let it cool; and do this to the patient every week once with other good treatment, until he is healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Or if you wish, cauterize him by making several points with the entire cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This manner of cautery moistens the brain evenly; and then place on it cotton soaked in butter and chicken fat.
de l’awe des eulz	of the water of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When water first comes to the eyes, by the signs that I have mentioned in the division, then begin and give the patient something to drink that cleanses the head, and protect him from all moisture, and make him sweat in a bath several times while fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	Afterward, have him shave the back of his head, and make a cautery in the middle of the head, and make two cauteries on the two temples if the flow of water is in both eyes, or one if the flow is in one; and with the cautery burn all the veins and arteries that are below the heart, and let the cauteries be long according to the width of the temple; and beware of excessive bleeding, and if you see too much blood coming out, staunch it with such power as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and in the incision the precaution of how you will staunch it; and sometimes one makes a cautery or cauterization below the two bones behind.
dou cors des larmes	of the body of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	When the tears of the eyes are long-standing and habitual and are on the veins, or near the arteries that are visible on the outside of the head; and one sees that it is from cold phlegmatic superfluities, then make the cautery that I mentioned at the beginning of the water descending to the eyes: one cautery in the middle of the head, and two cauteries on the two temples, and two cauteries or cauterizations below the two bones; and if there is more need, cauterize it carefully above the eyebrow with a small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	of the body of tears inside the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you treat it according to what we have said in the section, and it does not help, then give the patient to drink for three nights boiled things; afterwards shave the head, and make a cautery in the middle of the olive-shaped cautery; and make two cauteries of the cautery which is called "clavilis" on the two eyebrows, a little below the hair; and beware of the artery so that you do not cut it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the shape of the cautery which is called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the eyelid is softened by illness and moisture, then cauterize it with this cautery, which is called "olivare". (or "olive-shaped")
de coi ci est li forme:	of which here is the form:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you wish, make two cauteries on the two eyebrows as long as the eyebrows are; and do not remove the hand until a third of the eyelid is burned, in the manner I have described.
dou poil qui point l’oil	of the hair that pricks the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	Sometimes it happens that the eyelashes turn inwards and prick the eye, and for this, cauteries are made in two ways: namely with fire, or with a burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they grow and are even, then place the patient on your lap; then draw on the eyelid a figure like a myrtle leaf, and let the beginning of the mark be near the hairs; then put cotton moistened with egg white and psyllium mucilage on the eye, then heat the cautery which has this shape:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cauterize the figure you have drawn little by little many times, so that the flesh is burned there; and the sign of the success of the procedure is that you see the eyelid retract, and the hairs raised at the edge of the eye; then remove your hand, and leave it thus for three days, then put cotton moistened with butter until the burn is healed; then treat it with ointment until it is healthy.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if after this the hairs return and the eyelid is softened, then repeat the cautery on the same spot, as you did the first time; and if the hairs are destroyed, cauterize it until the eyelid is raised to its natural position, and is even, and the hairs do not prick the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The cautery of burning medicine is that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even, then make a myrtle leaf shape out of parchment; then take French soap and quicklime, one ounce of each, and grind them together well; and do it quickly, so that it does not cool, then spread it on the shape you have made like a myrtle leaf, and place it on the eyelid; and if the patient has it in only one eye, you should work on one, and if in both, likewise; and place cotton moistened with egg white under the eye; and let the patient's head be on your lap and put your index finger on the medicine, and press a little and move it every time the patient feels the medicine burning, because it feels like fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a while, remove the medicine with your finger.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the burning sensation has passed, lift the spot with water, and look to see if you see the eyelid raised as if it had been raised by the force of fire or by incision; and if it is so, it is good.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If not, then apply more medicine to the place where the medicine has not worked, until your work is even and your eyes are aligned; then apply cotton moistened with butter until the burned skin falls off, afterwards treat the area with the ointment called "dyafenis" and others, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And you must take great care in your work, being very careful that none of the medicine falls into the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if the eyelid becomes soft afterwards, and the hairs prick the eye, reapply the medicine to the softened area of the eyelid, just as you did before; then treat it until it is healed; and this is the shape of the myrtle leaf:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that people's eyes are different in size, and your restraints should be adjusted accordingly; and the right way is not revealed to one who is studying this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	on the treatment of fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have described in the sections on diseases, and your treatments are not effective, then you must cauterize it in this way.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to place their head in your lap; and the practitioner should hold their head between their hands in such a way that they cannot move or shake their head; then place cotton moistened in egg white or purslane juice on the eye; then heat the cautery, which is like this: and is shaped at the end like the feather of a vulture, similar to how the cautery should be; if you wish, it may be pointed from one end to the other, or if you wish, it can be like a tent; however, this one that is shaped is better for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	Then squeeze the fistula if it is open, and draw out the pus, and dry it; and if it is closed, open it, and draw out the matter; then apply the very hot cautery, and hold your hand on the cautery on the side of the nose above the eye, so that your hand does not make a mistake; and place the cautery in the fatty tissue of the eye, and destroy it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you reach the bone at the beginning of the cauterization, that would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, repeat the cauterization once more, and again if needed, and leave it for three days; then apply cotton soaked in butter, and treat it with the desiccative ointment until it is healed, and if forty days pass and it is not healed, apply a sharp corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed; and treat it according to what is appropriate in its chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a method of cauterizing a fistula that some of the ancients described.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Make an incision in the fistula, and split the area; then put in the incision a thin reed whose form is as follows:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and make it the size of a lead weight of 3 [units]; and hold your hand or the reed firmly, and the patient should not move at all, so that the melted lead does not run into his eye; and it is necessary to place over the patient's eye cotton soaked in egg white or water: the lead burns the fistula site, and heals it with marvelous efficacy.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cauterization we have described, that is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, then it is necessary to administer medication through the syringe and return the fistula to the body of the syringe as appropriate to its proper place.
des crevaices en levres	of cracks in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Very often cracks occur in the lips, which are called "poil" (hair), and especially in the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks with what we have described in the sections, and the treatment is not effective, then heat a small knife-shaped cautery as follows:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it quickly into those cracks until it reaches the bottom; afterward treat the area with a cerate until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess arises at the base of the throat or in the uvula, or on the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, it subsequently festers and rots and ages and becomes a fistula; and you treat it as we have described in the sections, and it is not at all effective: then you must take a cautery according to the size of the fistula; then insert it into the opening of the fistula, and hold your hand there until the hot iron reaches the bottom of it, and the furthest point; and do this once or twice, then treat it with what we have described in the treatments, until it is healed; and if it is healed thus, it is good; and if not, then it is necessary to uncover the area and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	of the movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth are loose, and you treat it with medicines and it is of no use, then place the patient's head in your lap; then heat the cautery whose shape will be given later in such a way that you place a link on the tooth; and apply the hot cautery quickly inside, and hold your hand there until the patient feels the heat reaching the root of the tooth; then remove your hand and reapply the cautery as you wish; afterwards have the patient fill his mouth with salt water, and hold it there for an hour and then spit it out. 
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this way the tooth that was loose is strengthened, and the softened gum tightened, and the corrupted moisture dried.
de la dolor des dens	of the pain of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When toothache comes from cold, where there is cold or a worm, and medicinal treatments are ineffective, then cautery is necessary in two ways: cautery with butter and cautery with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cautery with butter is such that you take cow's butter, and melt it in an iron or brass spoon; then take cotton and wrap it around the tip of a tent, and soak it in boiling butter, and apply it quickly to the aching tooth and hold it there until it cools; and do this often until its virtue reaches the root of the tooth, and if you wish also soak wool and cotton in cold butter, and place it on the aching tooth, and apply a hot iron until the heat reaches the end of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	The cautery with fire is as follows: you take a rod of iron or brass, thick enough so that the fire does not reach the patient's mouth; then heat the cautery, the shape of which will come later, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand there until the cautery cools; do this often, for the pain will be removed that same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And the patient must fill his mouth with good butter immediately after this cautery, and then spit it out; and this is the shape of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make the cautery with whichever end you wish, and according to what you are able to do; and this is the shape of the rod:
des scrophules	of scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When scrofula results from phlegm and cold humors, and does not respond to digestion by medicines, then heat the pointed cautery, the shape of which follows, and it should have two openings for the fumes to escape from the cautery on the other side; and place the hot cautery on the swelling once, or twice if necessary, until it reaches the bottom of the swelling; and if the swelling is small, apply the cautery according to the size of the swelling, and leave it thus for three days; and apply cotton soaked in butter until the burn is gone; then treat the area with ointments and dressings until it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	The shape of the rod:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When the humors overcome the bronchial tubes of the lung, and especially when this comes from a cold complexion, then the patient must first be purged by laxative medicines; then cauterize him at the base of the throat, and be careful not to go down to the throat itself, and do not burn the heart but only a little.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then make another cauterization at the joint of the neck at the top of the spine, and let the cautery be the one called "clavile," of which we have the form before; and treat the area as we have said before until it is healed.
de la toust	of the cough
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When a cough and lung disease are from cold humors, and the patient has no fever or dryness, and the illness is chronic, then make two cauterizations on the chest in empty places; and another cauterization in the middle of the chest between the two nipples; and let the cautery be the one called "clavile" according to the form previously described.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you wish, make a cauterization by pricking with the entire cautery which is called "points," of which the form is found earlier in the discussion of ear ailments; and let there be up to 30 pricks, or thereabouts.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	Afterwards treat the area according to what has been said before, and let the cautery have three prongs according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And because of this the cauteries are easier, because you make three at once.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	On the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	After, the patient should be laid on their back and on their side; then lift the core which is within the armpit with the fingers of your left hand; and if the joint is dislocated inwards, heat the cautery which has two prongs of which here is the form:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and cauterize the core until it pierces through to the rib, and the mark of the cautery would resemble four cauteries; and therefore, cauterize with the cautery which has three prongs, whereby the marks of cauterization are six cauteries; and the prongs are the thickness of a tent and this is the form of the cautery which has three prongs:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And sometimes another prong is added to this, whereby there are eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	Then apply crushed leeks with salt onto the cautery; then let the patient rest, and the limb should not be moved for a long time until it is well strengthened.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated upwards, which happens rarely, then apply cautery on the thick part of the collarbone, with many cauterizations by pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed, and the moisture is removed and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When coldness and much moisture enter the stomach, so much so that it draws it to its complexion, and catarrh increases in it, and customary treatments are used and they are not effective, then the patient should be laid on their back, and extend their legs and arms.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	After this, make three cauteries: one below the hollow of the chest by the width of a finger, with the whole cautery instrument; and two cauteries outside on both sides, so that the shape of the cauteries forms a triangle, and there is such a space between one and the other that they are not joined together when they discharge pus; and let the cauteries be so deep that they reach two parts of the heart, and the shape of the cauteries be according to this form without addition:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if you wish to cauterize with a large cautery in the middle of the stomach according to this shape; and for he who is afraid of this cautery, cauterize by pricking and mark a point on the stomach according to the amount of ink you wish; then cauterize it with the whole cautery which is called "pointed".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the ailment that we discussed before, until he is healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	When pain comes to the liver from cold and moisture and great flatulence, so much so that it is greatly removed from its natural complexion by the superfluities; and the patient is treated with what we have said in divisions, and it does not benefit him, then it is necessary that the patient be laid on his back; and mark with ink three cauteries according to this form and this figure and this size on the liver, outside the hypochondria, where the elbow comes; and there should be a space between each cautery the width of a finger; and the cauteries should be along the body, and do not press your hand too hard with the whole cautery; and only half the core should be burned, and let the patient be standing upright; and if he cannot, let him be lying down, and extend his legs, and raise his arms; and this is the form: 
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	And if you wish, cauterize these cauteries with the lancet, if you are skilled and wise in the art, and be careful not to burn the entire core, because you would dry out the whole body; and do not let it come to a boil, for the core is very delicate there, and know this for certain.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When there is an abscess on the liver, and you want to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the membrane: if it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain, but not too strong; and if it is in the membrane, he feels intense pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And then when this treatment requires the doctors, it is necessary that the patient be laid on his head; and then mark with ink the place where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery which is similar to a ray, of which here is the form:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And cauterize one cautery so that the core is burned, and it comes to suppuration, so that all the pus is out; afterward treat according to the treatment of issues until he is healed; and no one should use this cautery except someone who has studied long in the art of medicine, and through whose hands these illnesses have passed sometime.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Then he can operate boldly, and yet it seems to me that it is better to leave it alone.
dou cautere de pleuresin	of the cautery for pleurisy
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that for pleurisy one should make cauteries of birthwort root, and in this manner: take a long birthwort root, the largest that you can find, and let it be dry, and be as thick and as long as your fingers; and soak it in oil, and put it in the fire, and cauterize one cautery between the armpit and the neck, and two small cauteries a little descending on the part which is below the chin; and two cauteries between the fifth rib and the sixth, inclining a little behind; and one cautery in the middle of the chest, and another on the stomach, and one between the two shoulders, and two on the two sides of the chest outside the cautery which is between the two shoulders; and do not press your hand, but do it lightly as if smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And some ancients said that some men use a cautery of iron resembling a razor, and they heat it and put it between the ribs, until it comes to that abscess; and the pain leaps out, as we have said in the abscess of the liver. 
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this procedure, there is fear that the patient will die immediately, or a fistula will develop that cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the lamprey
