Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the lamprey disease using what we have mentioned in the divisions of treatments, and it does not help, then there are three appropriate types of cautery that are all good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	Of which, one method is that you make three cauteries, or four, in a line along the length of the lamprey, following the pattern of the cautery of the liver that we have discussed before; and do not press your hand with all the cautery, and let the patient lie frequently on his back; and another method of cautery is that you heat the cautery that has two prongs, as we have shown it in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the skin that is around the lamprey, where the patient's side is on the left, and let the elevation by which you lift the skin be parallel to the length of the body and the cauteries be across the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	Then put the two heated prongs in until the skin is pierced on the other side, and then pull out the cautery, and thus there will be four. And if you want, cauterize using the three-pronged cautery.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	Use this treatment after the patient has expelled pus for a long time, and this is better than the other treatments mentioned before.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cautery is not useful for dropsy, except in the manner which is called "ascites".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you treat it according to the methods we have described in divisions, and your treatment is not effective, then you must make four cauteries around the groin, and one on the stomach, and one on the liver, and one on the spleen, and two behind the back on the spine, and one near the chest; and the cautery should be very close to the thickness of the skin.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	Afterwards, leave the cautery open to drain pus for a long time, and do not abandon the treatment of the patient after the cautery; and healing will be hastened, and the two intentions will be combined with God's help.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The shape of the cautery for the belly should be the key-shaped one that we have previously shown; and that for the back should be olive-shaped, according to what has been stated before.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the feet are swollen in someone who is dropsical, and are full of citrine-colored water, you must cauterize on the back of the foot between the little toe and the ring toe; and lift your hand with the cautery without turning.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not go in too deep, thus the citrine water will come out, and the cautery should be of this shape:
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	Afterward, make two cauteries on each leg, on the shin bone; and the cautery should be long, one below the knee in front and the other outside, in the middle of the leg; and leave the cauteries open for a long time without treatment, so that the water comes out; after, treat them like the other treatments that we have mentioned.
de la menoison	of menstruation
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	When diarrhea comes from cold and moisture, so much so that the retentive and digestive power which is in the stomach and in the intestine is weakened, and cannot be treated by any means of treatment; and you see the patient suffering greatly and of strong constitution, make a large cautery on the stomach according to what has been discussed previously on cautery of the stomach, with the circular cautery; and four cauteries around the navel, small, with a small key-shaped cautery, and two cauteries on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see abundant moisture and the patient suffering, make a cautery on the wrist, and a cautery on each flank, and two small cauteries on the stomach near the large one, because the treatment is beneficial when there is good assistance.
de la cure des emorroydes	of the treatment of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When the hemorrhoids are in the anus, one or more, and are old and are from gross cold and moist corrupted humors, and are treated as we have said in divisions, and it is not effective, then make cauteries: three on the spine, the one that is furthest out below the shoulder blade little by little in a triangle, and one cautery below the navel two fingers; and if you think that their stomach is chilled, and the food is not digested, and one sees swelling in the face, then make a large cautery on the stomach, as mentioned before, and another on the liver, and another on the spleen with the key-shaped cautery; and leave the cautery open for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After, treat the area until it is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshy growth which is called "thelul" (a fleshy growth or polyp)
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut the fleshy growth, heat the cautery which resembles a razor, and then place it, burning hot, on the cut fleshy growth; and keep your hand there until the cautery reaches the base of the vein from which the blood flows; do this once or twice, and if there are many fleshy growths, cauterize each one as we have said; afterwards treat them with beneficial ointments until they are healed; and if you cauterize with a large cautery on the ischium, it will be more helpful.
de plaie mal curee	of a poorly healed wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot bear cutting or opening, which we will discuss in its place, such an illness arises that can only be healed by cautery. 
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When someone develops a fistula, and it is aged and emits pus and corrupted fluids, you should probe it fully with a thin tent, and make sure you know, using the whole tent, how deep it is.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	Then heat the cautery that resembles a razor, and insert it into the fistula to the depth the tent entered, and repeat the cautery until the rotten and corrupted flesh is burned, once, twice or thrice, according to the need; and be careful not to burn the nerves that are nearby, and the large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	If the fistula goes to the body of the bladder and to the intestine, beware of these places, and do not do this except in fleshy areas, and be sure it is not perforated; afterwards treat the area until it is healed, and if the place is sealed, and the matter is removed over time, then know that the place is completely healed; and if the matter is not removed, know that the place is perforated, and the bone at the bottom is corrupted; and so as one of those which we will discuss in its place. 
de la maladie des reins	Of the disease of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain from cold comes to the kidneys, and from great flatulence, and there is no desire for women, then you must cauterize him on the kidneys on one side and the other with the key-shaped cautery that we have mentioned before; and if we cauterize him in the middle, he will have three cauteries in a line, and they will do more good. 
de la vessie	Of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then cauterize him on the outside above the bladder, where the pubic hair begins, one on the right and one on the left, and let each cautery be as long as the joint of a thumb; and make a cautery on the outside of the back, or two if you need to; and let the cautery be key-shaped according to the aforementioned form.
de la marris	Of the womb/uterus
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the womb is cold and moist, and yet does not fail to conceive, and the menses are corrupted and their periods delayed; and when they come, she feels great pain: then it is necessary to make three cauteries around the vulva, as we have said for the cauterization of the bladder, and two cauteries on the outside of the back; and let the cautery be key-shaped, as we have said. 
de la hainche	Of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When viscous humors descend to the hip socket, and for this reason it moves out of place, and the sign is that the thigh is longer than the other when they are measured together; and the place of the separation is found empty, it is necessary that you cauterize the patient on the hip socket with a cautery resembling a circle, and mark in front around the socket as it turns, so that the socket is inside the circle; and let the cautery be like the one with which the stomach was cauterized.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cautery is not available, make three large olive-shaped cauteries, and let the cautery be as deep as the skin; and treat it until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	Of the pain of the hip
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the hip socket, and it is from cold and moisture, and the patient is treated as we have said in the section [on dislocations] and the treatment is not effective, and the illness is old: then you must purge the patient of the thick humors with foul-smelling pills, or other similar good pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	Afterwards, make a cautery; and the method of cautery is according to two methods: that is to say, with burning medicines together, and fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cautery is of many kinds, one of which is as follows: that you cauterize on the hip socket three triangular cauteries in this shape, and make them good and deep, and have between each cautery a space the width of a finger, and let the cautery be olive-shaped; sometimes one makes a cautery in the middle on top of the hip, which makes four in this shape:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you wish, cauterize it with the circular cautery that we mentioned earlier in the dislocation of the hip; but do it in such a way that the circle contains the whole hip, and all the thickness of the flesh is burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the method used in sciatica, when the pain is in the hip, and does not reach down to the thigh or the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it reaches the thigh and leg, make two cauteries where the patient says the pain is, and one cautery above the ankle by four fingers, slightly to the left side; and let the cautery be knife-shaped, and let the thickness of the flesh be burned; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to the toes of the foot or almost there, cauterize it where they feel the pain, three or four points with the cautery called "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if necessary, make more; and if it is known that the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, make a cautery with the knife-shaped or circular cautery, and take good care in all your cauteries not to leave the cautery so long that you burn the nerves and the large arteries, and that you do not cause the patient further harm and contraction. 
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen several who have made a cautery on the ankle of the foot, and left it so long that the leg was all swollen, and the foot too, and the whole foot was pierced and corrupted.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a bowel movement from which he died.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pain is in two places together, make a cautery in one and the other, in this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the wise men said, regarding the cautery of the hip, of which here is the method: make such an iron, and let it be at the tip as thick as a fingernail, or a little less, and let it be between notches, and from one notch to the other the distance of a thumb joint; and let the notches be open on two sides, and be like knots, and let there be a well-made iron handle; and this is the form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let it be heated until it is all red and throws sparks, and then place it on the joint of the diseased hip, and turn it toward the healthy side; and cauterize once in a round cautery and leave it for three days; and then make a plaster of butter, and leave the wound open a long time; then treat with ointment until healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasis says that we use this cautery little because of fear of its appearance, and we see few who use it; and yet it is one of the good cauteries, for those who can bear it, and where it is appropriate.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The cautery of burning medicine is that you make an instrument with notches into which the lip of the opening descends, and it should be of brass or iron with a long side, and at the top have two knots, and between each the distance of the thickness of a finger; and let them be open below and above, and join together according to this form:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	Then place it on the hip joint of the patient lying on his healthy side, and press your hand firmly on the hip joint; then pour between the two circles hot water that has been heated a little on the fire, and leave it for an hour, and let the patient endure the heat and the burning from it.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it will find there a bite as if from fire; and when the burning has passed, remove your hand with the instrument and wash the hip with fresh water, and leave it thus for three days, and apply butter until what is black from the burn is removed; and leave it three days so that the rot comes out; and this should be the last resort after treatment with ointments until healed.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain extends down to the thigh or to the leg, make an instrument for it that holds water just as you made for the hip; and this is the method of hot water, and I have written it in the treatise on the correction of medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alkali and quicklime, equal amounts of each, and grind them together, and put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	where there is a small hole below so that the point of a razor can enter; and place on top of this pot another well-sealed pot, and put alkali and lime and fresh water on top, until there is a finger's width above the powders when you have pressed it well with your hand; and leave it thus until sharp water descends and falls into the sealed pot, then take all this water, and pour it over lime and alkali as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And then it will be very sharp and is administered in many medical procedures and in cauterizations of other limbs. For it acts like fire, and there are other medicines with which one cauterizes the hip well, such as copper sulfate and anacardic honey and lime with soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galen tells us of a cure by which a man was cured of hip pain and sciatica, and praises it highly, and says that no other treatment was done, and that he was healed at once when this cure was performed, and he had bathed as he instructs below.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And he says in this way that you take fresh, dry green litharge, and grind it well with a little grease, and put it on the hip and on the thigh and on the leg where the pain is, and bind it; and leave it for three hours or for as long as the patient no longer feels the burning.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then have him enter the bath until his body is a little moistened, and have him go to bed, and the pain will go away completely and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use cautery with such medicines, unless it is after purging the body.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat dung, it helps a lot; and the cautery should be done in this way.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take wool and soak it in old oil, and put it on the hollow that is between the big toe and the next one which is called foscile. 
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	Then take dry goat dung, and light it on fire until it becomes coals, and put it on the wool, and leave it until it is extinguished; and do it again like this, and do not stop doing this until you think by reason that it reaches the hip, and that the pain has ceased; and this type of cautery is called "goat cautery".
de la dolor dou dos	of back pain
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, either by falling or by a blow, or by too great an evacuation, or by some spread of cold matter, for none of these cases is cautery useful, except for the one that comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary after the patient has been purged with foul-smelling pills or other such, that three lines marked with ink be made on his back where the pain is, and on each line five cauteries or more according to the strength and amount that the patient can bear; and let the cautery be done according to the cautery which is called "points"; and if you wish, make three or four cauteries with a medium key cautery according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this disease comes to small children, and the sign of the beginning is that they have restricted breathing when they stand up, and fear; and you find on the last spinal process of the back and around it the appearance that comes on the other spinal processes.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you want to treat it, cauterize it with a circular cautery in this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So that the cautery affects each part of the spinal process equally.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you wish, cauterize around the spinal process with the point cautery, two or three lines, and let the points be close to each other.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	Afterward, treat the area until it is healed according to what we have said, and be careful not to apply cautery to a gibbosity which is in a spasm of the nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When joint pain is from moistures that are spread to each limb of the body, and when the pain comes in the feet, which physicians properly call "podagra" (gout), and when it is from a cold cause and medicinal treatments cannot cure it, it is cured by cauteries in this way: make many cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to this form: 
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if it is necessary that you prick on the surface of the foot, then make a cautery with the entire cautery that is called "point". (or "pointed")
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains reach the knees and other joints, and this happens often, make three or four cauteries on each knee, on each side, with the olive-shaped cautery; and if you need more, make more, but do not hold your hand there longer than it takes for the thickness of the skin to be burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend to the knee and to the back, administer the cautery that we have described in its chapter. 
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, make points around the wrist in two lines; and if any pain remains in the fingers, make points on each joint and on the back of the hand; and if the pains reach the elbows or up to the shoulders, cauterize each part, and ensure the patient has good care and takes medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you give him good care and you purge the phlegm, he will be healed with God's help.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the peritoneum/abdominal wall
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When a rupture occurs in the groin, and the intestines descend into the scrotum, and it is recent, it is necessary that when you see to treat it, that he does not eat anything that day; and that he consumes things that loosen the bowels, so that the feces descend from his belly; afterward, have him sit on his back between your hands, and tell him to hold his breath until the intestines are replaced, and put them back with your fingers, and make an incision below the rupture on the pubic bone, and another incision that resembles half a circle above the body; then heat the cautery, of which this is the shape:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	until it is white and throws sparks.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then put the intestines back in their place; and let the assistant hold his hand there so they don't return; and open the patient's thighs well, and place a cushion under him and an attendant on his thighs, and another on his chest who holds his hands; then place the cautery on the incision with your whole hand, and hold it straight and hold it until you reach the bone, and if you don't reach it the first time, do it again until you reach the bone; and be very careful that the intestines do not protrude when you apply the cautery; so that you do not burn them; and that because of this the patient does not die, or suffer other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is worthless.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And the cautery for children must be small according to their size, and for adults, large according to their size; after three days treat the cauterized area with butter until the burning sensation is gone; then treat it with other ointments until it is healed, and let the patient lie on his back for forty days until the wound is well closed; and his food should be easily digested for a long time, so that the intestines do not protrude when he gets up to go to the toilet.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when he wants to get up, provide him with a well-made bandage, and he should wear it for another forty days; and he should have good rest, and work little and avoid overfilling himself with drink and food, and shouting too loudly; and when he follows these instructions he will be completely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will discuss the treatment of cutting in its own chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the abdomen/belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures appear in other bellies and are recognizable, and you see that they are not growing larger, make a round cautery burn according to its size, and let a third of the core be burned; afterwards treat it as we have described; and some of the ancients have said that it should be cauterized with a three-angled cautery in this way:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	But first mark the place with ink and make a line across the width above the rupture, and another outside it, and hold your hand in the middle with the heated cautery.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauterization is lighter and gentler.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes in a limb, either from a fall or a blow, and this pain lasts a long time, and medical treatment is of no use, then it must be cauterized with the cautery which is called "points," and the cauterization should be according to the length of the limb and its smallness and weakness and its strength and location of the twisting pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If he is healed from the first cauterization, that's good; if not, repeat another cauterization over it, because it is customary that it should move to the limb that is nearest to it, so you must do the cauterizations until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	of leprosy
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	Lepers are sometimes helped greatly by cautery, and especially the illness that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	When you see it fit to cauterize, take note if the illness is at the beginning, and if it has been treated according to what we have said in the division, and it neither descends nor remains, and you fear that the corruption will take hold of the whole patient, then make five cauterizations on the head: one in the middle of the head at nine, and the other towards the forehead at the hairline; and two on the two temples, and one behind on the occiput; and leave your hand there so long that the cautery reaches the bone, and so that the scabs come out so that the vapors of the thick humors can escape; and cauterize on the back according to what is written above.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules; et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	And if the leprosy is spread everywhere and it appears manifestly, you must cauterize it with these cauterizations that we have mentioned on the head, and one cauterization on top of the nose, and two cauterizations on the spine of the neck, and six cauterizations on the spine of the back, and one large one on the rump and another next to it, and two on the two shoulders; and two on the elbows, and two on the tendons of the breast, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the palms of the hands; and beware of the nerves that are on the heel, that you do not burn them; and sometimes one makes a cauterization on the pubic bone, and another on the breastbone, and another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that the more cauterizations you make, the more help you give, and the more it benefits the patient; and know that the sick person does not feel pain from the cautery like healthy people feel it, because the body is already corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And the cauterizations must be large and small according to the limbs and joints, as you will find it in the forms of the irons.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	Afterwards, treat the area with vetch flour with honey and other treatments until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When a swelling appears on a limb and is treated with medicines and oils and plasters, and it is not healed, then cauterize it on the limb according to the size of the limb; and let the cauterization go a little deep into the flesh; then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And sometimes cauterization is done on the hand and on the foot and on the back, at the exit of the nerve that moves the limb, and thus the swelling is removed; however, no one should undertake this unless they are knowledgeable about the limbs and the exits of the nerves that move the body.
de albaras	of white leprosy (or vitiligo)
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is chronic, and medical remedies are of no use, then cauterize it with a somewhat deep cautery, according to the thickness of the flesh, until the whiteness is removed, and its color is changed; then treat it with vetch flour and lentil flour with rose oil and plantain leaves, and dove's blood and lark's blood, one part of each; and let it all be mixed together, and bound with a cloth, and applied to the area until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment of canker sores by cauterization
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a canker sore first appears, and you want to stop it, cauterize it with a cautery that resembles a circle, all the way around the canker sore. 
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And yet, the wise say that one should also cauterize in the middle of the canker sore; however, this does not seem good to me, for I fear that it may become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen this happen sometimes; and it is more appropriate that it be cauterized around it, with the cautery called "circular," as we have said regarding cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	Regarding swelling that cannot mature/come to a head
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When someone has a condition called "adubelati," and it is slow to mature or come to a head, either because of excess matter it produces or the age of the patient when he is decrepit (that is to say, very old) and he has little blood, or because of the weather; and you wish to hasten its maturation: then cauterize around it with many small cauteries, pricking; afterwards leave it alone.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it will hasten to mature/come to a head.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you want to pierce it completely with the cautery, then heat the cautery which has this shape:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And place your hand in the middle of this condition called "adubelati" until the cautery has pierced the core, and let the cautery be such that the patient feels it on the outside in such a way that the flow of pus is facilitated. 
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Afterwards treat it until it is completely healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	The treatment with fire by iron (cautery)
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	There is another type of disease which is called "corrodens," and it is nothing other than a consumption of the limb, for it eats away at the limbs as fire does dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in a place that can tolerate cautery with fire, then heat cauteries, both small and large nails, according to what is suitable for the place where the disease is; then cauterize it on all sides until you eradicate all the corruption, and nothing of it remains, so that all that is corrupted is removed. 
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then leave it for three days, and apply on the cauterized areas ground sulfur with oil until the burns from the fire are removed, and all the corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	Afterwards treat it with ointments that generate flesh.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if you see after three days that healthy flesh is not growing, that's good; and if not, then repeat the cautery on what remains of the corrupted areas.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this affliction has sometimes been treated with sharp medicine instead of fire cautery; but nevertheless fire cautery is of greater help, and I have already explained the treatment with the sharp medicine in the section: take it when you need it. 
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of the chilblains that come on the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Very often it happens that on the outside of the feet a malady arises which is called "corn" according to our understanding, and it is a large, misshapen thing that injures the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cauterization of this malady is done in two ways.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	That is to say, cautery by fire, and cautery by hot water.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cautery is done by heating a cautery iron like a vaulting rib, and it should be made of good iron of a size that it can enclose the corn on all sides, and that it has thin edges; then place it hot upon the corn, and turn your hand all around the corn until it reaches the bottom of the corn; and leave it thus for three days until it begins to discharge pus; then make a poultice of wild mallows ground with salt, and leave the poultice on all night, and the corn will fall off and be uprooted.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the area with an ointment that generates flesh until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are turned outwards on the body, and often this happens on the hands and feet, then you must apply cautery with hot water; and it is done in this way: take a tube of copper or iron, or a vaulting rib, and place it over the corn and the wart, that is to say, verrucous warts; and place the tube over it so that it surrounds it completely, then put in a little hot water, and hold your hand firmly, and press your hand while turning so that the edge of the tube reaches the root of the corn, and the hot water can find a deep path to the root; and let the patient endure the burning of the hot water for an hour; then leave it like that, and it will uproot itself completely with all its roots. 
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Do this one after the other, until you have extracted all those that are on the body, then treat them with ointments that generate flesh.
li cure dou trembler	The treatment of tremors/shaking/shivering/palpitations (depending on context. Could also be "trembling sickness" like Parkinson's disease, etc.  More context would be needed)
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee; et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When someone trembles from coldness of the nerves, or from quartan fever or other, then you must make four cauteries or four on the spine of the back, one cautery between each vertebra; and one cautery on the feet, and one on the stomach with olive cautery; thus the trembling will cease, and the health of the cold illness will hasten.
des pustules puans	Of/about stinking pustules/boils/sores
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Sometimes swellings or stinking pustules appear outside the body, which come from large corrupted matters.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	So it is necessary, at first when they appear, to make a cautery on each head of the pustule: a subtle cautery of myrtle wood, the tip of which is set on fire, or of long birthwort root, or with a lenticular cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And sometimes they are cauterized at the beginning when they appear, in this manner, and they cannot grow from then on, but the superfluity from which they come is broken, and they are healed; but this must be done after bloodletting.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times large flows of blood occur from the artery which is cut in a wound that comes to the surface, or in the incision of an abscess, or in the cautery of a limb, and in similar things; and it is a very difficult thing to stop.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And nevertheless, when this happens to someone, hurry to put your index finger on the wound of the vein, and press it hard until the blood is calmed under your finger, and no more drops come out; then put several small and large olive-shaped cauteries in the fire until they are all red; then take one, either large or small depending on the wound and the place where the artery is broken, and put the cautery on the vein where you hold your finger, and hold the cautery there until the blood is stopped.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it spurts out when you lift your finger from the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, quickly take another of the cauteries that are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to do this one after the other until the blood is stopped; and be careful not to burn the nerve that is nearby, and that no other harm comes to the patient; and know that when blood flows from the artery, it cannot be easily stopped, especially when the artery is large, unless it is by one of the four ways that we have mentioned: either by cautery, or by extraction when it is not severed, or by tight tying with thread, or by medicines applied that have the power to stop blood; and let it be tied and constricted properly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever would attempt to stop it by tightly binding with cloths or by putting burning things on it, or other similar things, will benefit little if at all. 
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to someone and they do not have a doctor or medicine present, they should put their index finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and press firmly until it is stopped over the wound and over the vein; and do not move the finger, but wet it with cold water, very cold water, often until the blood is congealed and thickened and stopped; and from then on do what is necessary with cauteries and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of surgical treatments.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter every illness in which cautery by fire, or burning medicine, is necessary, and the reasons and the causes and the instruments and the forms of cauteries; and I have arranged this chapter from head to foot, and I will go in this chapter by this same path so that one finds more easily what one wants.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And before I begin this, it is necessary, dear son, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first on cauteries, and therefore greater caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you not to undertake folly.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many kinds of people come for treatment.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	Some come who are so angry with their illness that they die easily from the fury they find in their disease, and from the greatness of its malice; and of these one must be wary. 
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And of these there are some who deceive you, saying, "Wait, I am cured"; and the illness is treacherous.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	You must not agree with those who come to you with this attitude, but put more emphasis on your honor than on your greed, and do not act foolishly but wisely in what you are certain of, and from which you can gain reward and praise; and use prognostication and indication in the treatment of your patients, to whom health is restored; and this will help you to acquire a good reputation, and glory, and a memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, May Our Lord give you good understanding and righteousness, and may he inspire you with the holy inspiration of his hand, amen. 
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Now I have arranged this chapter by dividing it into chapters, according to what is before in the chapter on cauteries, which I have described to you from head to toe, so that you can more easily find what you need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	of the head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this disease often comes to children at birth, and when the midwife squeezes the child's head too hard; and sometimes it comes from a hidden cause that is unknown.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease except in children, and in all those I have seen death came quickly; and therefore it seems to me that it is better for me to abandon the work in such treatments. 
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child whose head was full of water, and the head grew every day so much that he could not support it; and the fluid grew so much that he died, and this fluid had collected under the bone on the membrane, between the brain and the bone; and the procedure is as follows if the fluid is between the brain and the bone, and the abscess is small, that you make a wide incision in the middle of the head; and let it be as long as two nuts, so that the fluid flows; and here is the form of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the fluid is more abundant, and the abscess is larger, make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the fluid is under the bone, and the sign that you see is the sutures of the head open on each side, and the water spurts out when you press it with your hand inside, and this is not hidden from you: then you must make three incisions in the middle of the head in this way:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, draw out all the fluid.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After, bind the incisions with cloths and powders, and put in wine and oil, and leave it thus until the fifth day; then unbind it, and treat the wound with tents and ointments, and keep the head evenly bound, and give the patient dry food with little moisture until the limb is strengthened and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another method of incision is that you look where the size of the abscess and the collection of fluid appears; for sometimes it is in front; sometimes behind; sometimes on the right; and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Then cut there where the abscess appears, and where the fluid is collected, and make the incision according to what you are able to do; and be careful not to cut the artery; lest a flow of blood come, so that the patient dies from the loss of blood and the evacuation of fluid.
de reume	of rheum/phlegm/cold
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When someone experiences an illness called "catarrh" in the eyes or chest, and the illness is chronic, and medical treatment is not effective, then the last resort is cautery, along with cutting the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It is necessary, then, when you intend to cut them, that the patient tilt their head back; then rub the area with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then have the patient tighten their neck with a cloth; then look where the vein lies, and the location of both are behind the ears, and a little recessed; then mark the places with ink, then cut both with a sharp scalpel in two places, so that the cut goes down to the bone, and this should be across the width of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you wish, put the scalpel under the artery and cut it from above, cutting as you should, across.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, the blood spurts upwards continuously.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery is not apparent to the touch, then you must measure the distance of three fingers, then mark with ink and cut to the bone; and the necessary amount of blood to let out is six ounces, and perhaps a little more or less, depending on what the patient can tolerate, and the fullness of the artery; then examine the wound: if any membrane remains on the bone, cut it so that no abscess forms there, then bind and dress the wound, and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	of migraine
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When a chronic migraine occurs, and acute catarrh, due to the moisture of tears and heat in the temples and chronic raging dizziness and similar things, and it is treated by various medical treatments and all this is of no benefit, we should then open the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have described. 
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of their extraction is that the patient should shave back the hair from his temples, and locate the artery that is visible in the temple, for it is easily visible by its pulsation, and is rarely hidden except in some people who are excessively cold; and if it is hidden, the patient should tighten his neck with some cloth, then rub the area with some rough cloth, and sprinkle the area with hot water until the artery appears clearly; then take the scalpel which has this shape:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	then lightly score the skin until you reach the artery, then pull it up with forceps, and separate it well from the tissues that are underneath it on each side; and if the artery is thin, turn it with the point of a hook, then cut it from that side to the length of two grains of wheat.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not cut, the blood will not completely flow out.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw from six hundred to three hundred drops of blood; and if the artery is large, you must tie it in two places with a strong double silk thread, so that putrefaction does not occur before the wound heals, and bleeding occurs; then cut the excess between the two ties at that very moment, and then, if you wish, cauterize it with a bladed cautery down to the bone until the ends are cauterized; and this is the better practice, if the patient does not have a fever and he has a warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For cautery helps to dry out moisture: therefore it is of greater use for moistures.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Or, for the extraction of arteries, it is necessary to fill the place with old cotton and put well-made tents on it; and when they are removed, it should be treated with dry medicines that promote flesh growth, and with tents, until it is healed; and if blood flows from the artery while you are working on it, hasten to cauterize it, or fill the place with vitriol and press it with your hand so that the blood is stanched; and if you do not have that available, put your finger on the place until the blood clots, and sprinkle the area with cold water until the bleeding stops, and compress it as needed; and what is better and easier in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vessel with this cutting cautery on both sides, but the blades should be quite thick to retain their heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too thin, it holds its heat less well.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus; et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And there should be a finger's width of space between the two blades, and then when you have marked the two places with ink, you put the burning iron on it until it reaches the bone, and cut the vessel in two places; and let there be space between the two ends for it is not completely sealed with this cautery; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes are descending from the vessels that are on top of the head from heat, and the medical treatment applied is not effective, and you see the patient's face redden, and feel a throbbing in the forehead like a tremor; and his eyes are weak and watery so that the hairs of the eyelids have fallen out, and the eyelids are heated and chafed by the burning of the tears, then this treatment is needed.
