Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want a lot of blood, we start again often; and if the blood is thick, strike deeply, and the limit is that the skin be pierced suddenly, and for those who have thick and hard skin, and who have narrow pores, you should anoint the places for the cupping glasses with opening and dissolving oil: if it is in summer, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or oil of cucumber seed; and if it is in winter, with watercress oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluity is thick and cold, take oil of marjoram, or of balsamite, or oil of dill, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the one being treated has tender flesh and large pores, no oil should be applied, but they should be washed after cupping with rose water, or cold water, or nightshade water, or cucumber water, or purslane water, or similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has a lot of moisture, let him rise with vinegar, or myrtle water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have thick superfluities rise with old wine, or elder water, or a decoction of dill or chamomile, or other similar things; and one should not be cupped before the bath nor in the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two; and should not sleep after cupping, and it is necessary that he be careful, when he is to be cupped and when he has been cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And be wary if the one being treated is choleric, and if the blood is too sharp and inflamed; then he must take cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuces with vinegar, and similar things; and eat chicks, and mutton, and moist foods.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And he who has a cold complexion, let him take honey syrup, and moderately fragrant wine, which is between old and new, and eat little, and eat chicks and small birds and pigeons; and the day he is cupped, he should drink more than he eats; and it is necessary to sometimes give some men theriac or nutmeg before cupping, or after, to strengthen the principal members; and let the blood be thinned, but it is not necessary that those who are warm drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The cups that are placed without scarification are those that are placed on the liver, and on the spleen, and for gout, and on the belly and the buttock and the loins and the hip, because these parts do not tolerate scarification on the eyes, and it is only done with fire to draw blood from one part to another, as we place them on the breasts when the nose bleeds; to remove the viscosity that is in the part, as we place cups on the belly and on the buttocks to reduce the part; and remove the pain, when there is blockage or stone, thus it removes by its attractive power perhaps the blockage, or loosens the stone from its place; and so it does when it is placed on the liver and on the spleen when there is retained wind, and these cups are applied empty to only suck; and sometimes they are applied together with fire, and sometimes filled with lukewarm water, as in diseases of the pleurisy, and in such a way that the cup is filled with hot water alone, or with water in which suitable herbs have been boiled for this.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The method of cupping applied with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it should be two fingers wide and half a palm deep, and have on the side around the middle a small hole, just enough to insert a needle, and be made of brass, smooth in front so that it does not hurt the patient when placed on the limb; and have in the middle a crossbar of brass or iron, to place a lit candle, and they should be both large and small according to the illnesses and the age of those who receive them; for the cups for children are different than for the old, and for the thin than for the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one should place this cup on the limb thus: take the candle of wax or a wick, and place it in the middle of the cup across the bar which is in the middle of the cup, so that the flame is at the bottom of the cup so that it does not burn the patient; and then place it on the limb, and your finger should be on the hole that we mentioned, so that when one wants, the vapor escapes, and one removes the cup; and one takes the wick as before, and repeats it often, if you have need.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the cup then which is applied in the illness of pleurisy, with only water, there is no bar nor hole, and fire is not used except when it is full of water, and it is placed on the limb only; and this is the method:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Leeches are not used with fire except on limbs where one cannot place cups because of their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar places; and in places devoid of flesh, such as fingers or nose, and other similar; and the way to use them is that when you find leeches that are in clear fresh water without impurity, take them; and put them for a night in fresh water, until they are hungry, and have nothing in their bellies; and then be bled by vein or by cup, then rub the limb until it is red, and place the leeches on; and when they are full, and fall off, if it is a place where one can put a cup, put it there, for it is very beneficial afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, wash the place with vinegar, and then with water, very well, and then squeeze it; and if the place bleeds too much after the leeches' bodies, wet a linen cloth in cold water, and put it on, until the blood is stanched; and if the blood is profuse, apply ground vitriol, or gallnuts, and similar things, until it is stanched; or you put on the place halves of peeled beans, and leave them until they stick to the place, it will stop immediately; and if you need more, take other leeches.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the leeches do not want to attach, rub the place with fresh blood, or prick it with a needle until the blood comes out, and then put them on, and as soon as they smell the blood, they will attach; and when you see that they are about to fall off, sprinkle on a little aloe and crushed salt, or ash, they will fall off immediately.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that fools remove themselves from this chapter, because they have never seen any of the ancient books, nor read a letter of them; and for this reason science is diminished in our land, for I never found anyone good at it; and I know nothing about it, except through the knowledge of ancient books, where I have studied so much that I have drawn the science from them, and through experience, and through the practice of my life; and I have described for you in this chapter what is contained, and have summarized it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are used, as I have done in these two previous chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we state in the prologue of this book the main points of the discussion and the chapters where the wise man puts his understanding, and dwells on the truth, so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or sprain or bruise happens to someone, you must hasten to treat the patient on both sides, unless something prevents you entirely, such as weakness of the body, or infancy, or old age; or if the weather is not very hot, or too cold; and prescribe cold things, that is to say cold broths, and the meat of birds and kid, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not overfill with foods that fill the veins with blood, as long as you have no fear of a hot abscess, or of spreading of matter in the limb; then the patient should return to his former diet that he was used to.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary to nourish the patient with foods that make for substantial nourishment, where there is viscosity, such as wheat cooked in water, and rice, and heads, and feet, and cow's tripe, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with such nourishment the fracture heals better and faster.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the broken bones of the old and decrepit cannot heal or knit well according to their nature because of the dryness of the limbs, nor can those who are too tender, such as the bones of small children; but it doesn't matter, replace the broken bone with a large splint which holds and joins the limb together, until it strengthens as it was before; and do not stop its work, and for this reason it must be nourished with rich foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For a fracture of the head is different from a fracture of the chest, or of the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes across, and another obliquely, like the cut of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture with only a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each type has its own technique, and its own specific instrument for restoration, according to what comes to mind in its place; and the fracture of the bone is known because the place is twisted, and is clearly apparent by default, and sounds when pressed by the hand; and when there is no twisting nor sound when touched, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no fracture; but there can indeed be twisting, or a crack, or a small fracture. 
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	So you should not move it with your hand, but apply the medicines that follow, and then bind it carefully immediately.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that for the fracture that goes across, and the two parts are separated, you must immediately put them back in place evenly, before a hot abscess develops there; and if a hot abscess develops, leave it for a few days, until the abscess subsides; then set it as evenly as you can easily and wisely, and know that its restoration is easier than the restoration of one where there are fragments; then bind it, as is appropriate below.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if there are broken pieces in the bone, stretch it from both sides, if it is a hand or foot, or with your hand if it is a small limb, or with two cords, or with a cord and your hand; and place the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken limb are separated, bring the pieces back into their place as best you can, and be careful that your work does not cause injury or pain to the patient; and join the two ends of the bones well according to the best form.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it carefully with your hand if it seems to you that it is not right: then straighten it gently, and do not bind it too tightly, nor press it as those do whose work causes a hot abscess and contraction of the limb, as we have often seen.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is set, warn the patient carefully not to move it, neither waking nor sleeping, nor turning, nor in any other way; and make sure that the limb is so secure that he feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels no pain, it is not properly set, and it must be placed in such a position that he feels no pain; and be careful that it is placed straight, so that no crookedness occurs when it is healed; and the quality of the broken limb is according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs vary in smallness and size and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small limbs, such as arms and fingers and the like: these should be wrapped with bandages of soft and fine linen; and those that are large, such as the thigh and leg: these should be wrapped with a wide and strong bandage, for the wide bandage embraces the whole large limb, and constricts it evenly on all sides, so that there is no blemish; then tie around it light padding, three or four turns depending on the limb, and tighten your hand a little on the whole bandage, then go above the break and tighten less, further away from the break; and loosen the bandage little by little, until you cover a large part of the healthy area, then take another bandage, and wrap it again over the broken area; then go back to the part below the break, and tighten moderately, not too tight nor too loose, as we said in the first bandage above; then place between the bandages linen padding or cloths, until it is all even, then tie a bandage over it all, and then place your well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or an abscess, apply something soothing and warm for the abscess, and which removes the swelling, and leave it like this for a few days; then tighten your splints, and let them be half the width of a large, wisely cut dogwood branch, or of wood from which arrow shafts are made, or of palm branches, and let them be according to this figure: 
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	but the splint that is placed over the break must be a little thicker and wider than the others; and be as long as is necessary for the limb, whether small or large; then tighten over the splints as you did with the first bandage, then tie a thread over it appropriately, as in the first bandage over the break; tighter above, gradually less so; and the threads must be medium, neither too thick nor too thin, and be of soft linen; for if the threads are thick, as I have seen in the works of fools who make their bandages of twisted linen cords, and that is a great error, because the bandage cannot be even if it is too tight, and there should not be less than a finger's width between each splint.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is injured by the ends of the splints after tightening in healthy places, place linen padding or carded wool underneath them so that he is not injured.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the fracture, and the skin is broken, I will describe the treatment hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that you should not tighten all broken limbs with splints on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limb is large, splints should not be applied until after five or seven days, or more depending on your certainty of a hot abscess occurring; and here is the method for ancient plasters to restore fractures, dislocations, and sprains: take the flour that sticks to the walls of the mill, and mix it with plenty of eggs, and apply this mixture, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common way of making the plaster that restores fractures of many kinds, and especially for women and small children, because it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plaster restoring fracture, dislocation, and sprain: take three units of yellow sweet clover, labdanum, elecampane, and asafetida, and gum arabic, and galbanum, ten units each; myrrh and aloe, five units each; mastic nine units; and make a powder, and mix them with plenty of eggs; if the person's complexion is hot, use this plaster, because it is of good composition, and quickly restores broken bones, and is beneficial for many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another kind of plaster that is good for sprains: take galbanum and marshmallow, ten units each; myrrh and aloe, nine units each; acacia six units; Armenian bole ten units, and grind well, and mix with water or plenty of eggs, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another kind of plaster for joints and bones separated from their places, and soothes the resulting pain, and outgrowth of bone, and fractures: take new wool, and soak it in vinegar and cooked oil, and apply it to the area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not restore, but it is good for soothing a hot abscess, and effectively removes pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another kind of plaster that restores broken bones: take dried fig leaves, and ground ivy leaves, and grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another kind of plaster for the restoration of a bone fracture and to reduce the remains of the abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take marshmallow root, chamomile, violet flowers, vetch flour, one part of each; and grind them, and mix with wine, and if the limb is heated, mix it with moist coriander water, or water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another kind of plaster, stronger than the first, when a hard abscess comes during the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take marshmallow roots, and flax seed, pomegranate rind, sweet clover, and elderflower, and violet and chamomile flowers, equal parts of all; and grind them, and mix with salt water, or fresh water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that one should not put on the fractured limb to restore it anything but a cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else more, and says that it should be medium, neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And Galen thinks that one should put on the broken limb, to restore it, slightly warm, dry things, such as myrrh and aloe and frankincense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another type of plaster that is good for injury and pain: take mastic and cut human hair, or bird feathers, and marshmallow root, and salt in equal measure, and grind them, and make a plaster and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then unbind it a little later, and take care if the patient feels any pain, or if the bone has moved from its place; if not, do not unbind it for several days. And if pain comes to the area, or itching, without rest or swelling, then hurry, and unbind it, and remove the plaster immediately; and take a light cloth, and a moist sea sponge, and dip it in water, and wash the area, until the itching stops, and the pain is soothed; then let the limb rest for an hour, then apply dry wool, moistened in water or rose oil, and bind it overnight, until you are sure of a warm abscess; and the inflammation of the limb subsides, and the pain is removed, then begin the bandaging again gently, and a little plaster, and do not tighten it as much as before; and continue gently until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the warm abscess and redness and pain and swelling are completely gone, and you need plaster and bandages, then start again, as you did the first time, similarly.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if none of what we have said happens to the limb, do not unbind it until after three days or four or five or seven; and sometimes leave it for twenty days, depending on what is observed, until the break dries, and the joining of the flesh approaches; then tighten it more than before, and increase his food, as I have said before; and if you see the area drying out more than necessary, know that nourishment cannot reach it; then moisten it with warm tepid water, every time you unbind it, and this should be every third day, and loosen the bandage a little; by this work, then, nourishment flows to the limb, and quickly corrects what foolish physicians do, who set the limb crookedly: this is bad, and it is also dangerous work, and I see nothing else to do but to leave it and work correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of the various types of fractures
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many types of fractures, and various forms, and the causes are distinct; for there are fractures that are made by the blow of a sword, and the blow removes all the bone down to the syfac which is under the bone, as an axe or wood does; and therefore this type of fracture is called "hachure" (axe-like).
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword cuts the bone from above without piercing, and this type of fracture is called "absolue" (complete); and the wound of these two fractures is large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a blunt percussion, or a split or a blow from a stone, or from falling on a stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a piercing fracture, which reaches down to the membrane which is under the bone, or it is on the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And there is also a wound that is placed in the bone as fine as a hair, and the crack is small, and therefore this fracture is called "capillaire" (hairline); and also the wound which is made either by striking with a stone, or by falling, or by a similar thing, and causes the piece of bone to enter downwards, and the place is sunken as cauldrons do when struck; thus the stone enters inside. 
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more to those who have moist bones in their head, like a child's head; and it happens in all these types of fractures that small pieces are separated like splinters; and I will speak of them in their place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we recognize all types of fractures by the indentation above them, and the probing with tents, and by the corrupted flesh that is on top.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The similar hairline fracture is recognized because when the bone has been uncovered, and one rubs ink on it, the fracture appears black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the fracture, pay attention to the patient's accidents, and if you see any bad accident, such as vomiting bile, and loss of consciousness, and stretching, and inflammation, and acute fever, and the eyes coming out and becoming red, and other similar ones in several dispositions, then it cannot heal without a doubt. 
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you see no alarming accident, and you expect recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wounded first comes to you, and it is in winter, it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day, as early as you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, before the tissue under the bone is corrupted, and the accidents that we have mentioned occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the bone fracture reaches the membrane that covers the brain, you must cut the fractured part like this: and that is, you take the head of the wounded patient, and uncover the bone in all the ways that you can, and over the shape of the wound as gently as you can, and if bleeding occurs when uncovering the bone, or a hot abscess, help him with what is necessary, and that is that you fill the place with cloths soaked in rose oil; and let the wound rest until the hot abscess is soothed, and you are sure of the bleeding; then begin to remove the bone around it, and this is done according to two methods of work: one way is that you cut with a narrow incision in front, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make another incision larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is that you have a number of different incisions, some narrow and others wide, and pointed, and made of Indian steel; and work lightly, so that you do not injure the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is strong and hard, you must pierce it around, before you make incisions with drills, not so deep that they pierce through the skull bone, and it should have a margin or a circle on the tip, which prevents the point from passing through the bone; and you must have several of them, so that each one comes to its place in the thickness of the bone, so that you have drills for every head; and this is the form of the three types of drills:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The method for piercing around the fractured bone is that you place a drill on the bone, and turn it with your fingers until you know that the bone is pierced; then place the drill elsewhere a little further on, and so do all around, then cut with the incisors the space of bone that is between the holes, and do this as delicately as you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you remove the bone with your hand, or with some of the instruments that you have, such as forceps, pincers; and be careful not to touch the brain or the dura mater.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and removed the bone, you must cut the remaining bone fragment with another instrument similar to an incisor, but it must be thinner and more delicate than the other incisor; and if any small bones or scales remain, remove them gently with one of the instruments; then treat the wound with tents and ointments as we have described.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of working is the one that Galen describes, which is safer; and he praises it very highly, and these are his words.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	You must first uncover a part of the bone, where the fracture appears most, so that when you have uncovered that part, you will place under it the head of this lenticular incisor, of which this is the form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And it does not cut on one side, and the part is sharp on both sides, so that the cutting edge is towards the bone; then strike with a small mallet on it, so that you cut the bone lightly all around, and take good care of the membrane that is underneath; if it is attached to the bone, remove it gently, for it can be removed well without harm, and without fear. 
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone fracture does not penetrate to the membrane, and the bone is only cut on the surface, and there are small pieces, you must scrape this roughness, and remove the scales with a fine scraper of which you must have various sizes, to use in each place the most suitable, according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	So scrape first with large scrapers, and then with finer ones, and do not cease doing this until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hair-thin cuts and fine fractures, you must apply treatment according to its correction; and this is a thing not revealed to one who has not applied his study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the meninges are exposed, you must take a linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and place it on the wound; then take another cloth folded in two or three, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and put it over the first cloth; and do this as gently as you can, so as not to aggravate the meninges, then apply another bandage over it, and do not tighten it except enough to hold the wound only; and leave it like this for a day or two, until the inflammatory swelling has subsided, then untie it, and apply medications such as lily roots, and vetch flour, and incense powder, and aristolochia, and similar things; and make a powder of these things, and put it on the wound, and always apply cleansing medications without causticity; and ensure that the wound is always clean, that you do not leave the ointment there, nor let pus collect, for when pus collects on the membrane of the brain, it corrodes and rots it, and great harm comes to the patient; for when something caustic is put on the meninges, it blackens on top. 
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care then, if any bad accident happens to the patient, as we have said, it is undoubtedly doubtful.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if blackness appears only because of the medicine that was applied, which has such a property, then you must take one part honey, and three parts rose oil and soak a cloth in it, and place it on the meninges; then treat it with the appropriate methods of treatment until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes both parts of the nose above are broken, or one of them alone, for these are two bones; and the one below is cartilaginous, and does not break, but only bends or twists, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, you must insert your little finger into the nostril, and with your index finger and thumb from the outside, gently realign the fracture; do this gently, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the nose, and your finger cannot reach the place, then you should straighten it with the end of a somewhat thick stick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is in two parts, do the same, and hurry to restore it the first day if you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the hot swelling has subsided, then insert tents of linen cloth into the end of the nose, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or insert another one on the other side, if the break is there; and the tents should be so large that they fill the nostrils.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some restorers say that the tents should be moistened with butter and changed every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem good to me, but they should be moistened in a mixture of egg white and mill dust; then leave the tent in place until the bone is firm, and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes goose feathers are inserted into the nose instead of tents, with a soft cloth around them, which holds the break in place, and the patient breathes through them; now do whichever you prefer.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if hot abscesses develop in the nose while you are working there, apply cerate or cotton moistened with rose oil, or a little diachylon.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if hot abscesses do not develop, apply a cooling plaster made of sesame flour and incense powder, mixed with egg white, then put light compresses on top, and do not bind the nose; and if the break of the nose is small, and it is broken into small pieces, extract them with suitable instruments, then stitch the wound, and treat it with things that generate flesh and promote healing, such as suitable plasters and ointments; and if there is no wound inside the nose, treat it with tents, and insert lead cannulas until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the fracture of the mandible/jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible is broken underneath, and there is no external wound, and the break is internal only, and it is not broken in two, except perhaps fractured internally, then one can recognize it easily. 
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the break is on the right side, that you put your index finger in the patient's mouth; and if the break is in the left mandible, then put your right index finger in, and gently push the fracture inwards, and adjust it with the other hand from the outside, and make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the mandible is separated into two, then you must administer extension from both sides, until it is even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if loosening or breaking of the teeth occurs, secure them with a gold or silver or silk thread, then put cerate on the broken mandible, and put on a double cloth; and put on the cloth a well-made large star, or a piece of leather, evenly shaped, long and wide according to the mandible, and tie it on as tightly as you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the shape changes, untie it on the third day, and then readjust what has changed; and apply a plaster, made of mill dust with egg white or sesame flour, after you have removed the cerate; and put light wool over the plaster, and if the plaster dries and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until he is healed; many times he is healed in three weeks. 
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if hot abscesses develop, then administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, see if any piece of the bone has been removed; then carefully remove it with suitable instruments.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with a lancet according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and none remain, sew the wound, if it is large, and apply a suitable plaster to generate flesh, until it is healed.
de la forcele	Of the forceps/tweezers
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The clavicle often breaks anteriorly, towards the shoulder, and the fracture occurs in three ways: either it is broken and separated in two, and there are pieces, and it is the easiest to restore; or there is a fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the procedure is, when the fracture is without a wound, that you have two assistants, so that one holds the shoulder blade near the broken clavicle; and the other stretches the neck towards the side; then align the fracture with your fingers, so that the shape is as it should be, and there is neither a bump nor a depression.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to stretch more, place a round bolster of cloth, or wool, under the patient's shoulder, and let it be thick according to your need; and stretch and lift the clavicle, and press the bolster with your hand, so that you align the fracture as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the end of the clavicle outwards, because it goes inwards deeply, then the patient should lie frequently on his back, and put a medium-sized pillow under his shoulder, and let the assistant push the shoulder downwards, until the bone of the clavicle is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then straighten the fracture with your fingers, and if you find it shattered, then you must make an incision over it; and pull out the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot join because of any protrusion, then cut it with one of the incisors that you have; but make sure you place this instrument under the clavicle, to protect the periosteum.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and it resembles a spoon, and is not pointed, and is as wide as necessary, according to the size of the bone and the nature of the work; and it has two ends, as you see, and one is wide, and the other narrow, like the opening of the wound that you made when you extracted the bones; and when you are certain of a hot abscess, then sew the wound, and if the opening is small, or you suspect a hot abscess, then fill the wound with cloths and tents, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot abscesses develop there, soak a cloth in rose oil and vinegar and wine, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The binding of the bone, when it is without wounds and without incision, is that you apply to the bone a plaster of mill dust and egg white, and put light compresses on top, and put a splint under the armpit, if you need it; then take a very large bandage, a palm wide, then put a double cloth over the compresses and the plaster; then take a thin splint three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around this bandage, so that the ends of the bandage are hanging; and place the splint over the fracture, and turn the bandage over the neck, and under the healthy armpit, and under the injured armpit; and bring it back from each side, and when you see that the bandage holds the fracture properly, and you see clearly that the splint does not move over the broken bone, then check it every day, and when the bandage loosens, tighten it; and have the patient lie on his back, and when he sleeps put a small pillow under his armpit to raise the shoulder; this will alleviate the clavicle fracture by elevating the shoulder, or you can tie his arm to his neck, and do not untie it unless some bad accident occurs, for up to twenty days; then reapply the plaster, if you see that it is needed, and tighten it and leave it like that, until it is healed; and it is healed in twenty-eight days at most, and in fewer for some people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the fracture of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	It rarely happens that the shoulder breaks in a wide place or in the middle, and it is not known except by touch; so treat it according to the nature of the fracture, and reset it according to its natural form, in all the ways that you can; then place on the area mill dust with egg white, and light compresses, and put on a double cloth; then put on a wide and thin splint, a little wider than the shoulder, and if under the splint there is a hollow in any place on the shoulder, fill that hollow with linen compresses, so that the splint sits evenly; and then bind it tightly with a large bandage, so that the splint does not move from its place, and check the bandage every day; and every time it loosens, tighten it, and adjust the splint if it is out of place, and let the patient lie on his side; and the shoulder is healed in twenty or twenty-five days. And when this period is complete, untie it, and be confident, for this is not a bone that is easily dislocated.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of bone protrudes, and points under the skin, then cut over it and remove it, and do what we have described in the fracture of the clavicle to soothe a hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture of the chest
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The chest is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; but it often breaks further down.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it sinks downwards, and the patient feels great pain, and shortness of breath, and coughs, and perhaps vomits blood, and the hollow appears in the broken bone, and one can feel it clearly.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that the patient often lies on his back, and you place a cushion between the shoulder blades, then press on the shoulders, and bring together the ribs of both sides with your hands, and strive to put them evenly in all the ways you can, until the shape of the bone is as it should be; then place plasters and padding on a thin splint of willow, or other light wood, and wrap it in a cloth, and tie it over the broken bone, so that it does not move; and wrap the bandage around the back, and tighten it suitably, and check the bandage every hour, and if it loosens, tighten it; and if it needs to be undone, because of infection or itching that comes to the area, or pain or abscess, then hurry, and undo it, and remove the plaster, and address whatever has developed there in terms of treatment; then replace the plaster, and tighten it until he is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the fracture of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the fracture of the ribs only occurs in thick places near the back, and at the end inside, and they only bend because they are slimy; and one can feel it well on examination with the fingers.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is such that you set the fracture evenly, as is necessary.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply the plaster, and secure it with a splint, if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the fracture of the ribs is pointing inwards, the patient feels very great pain, and a pricking, as if from pleurisy, because the bone pricks the lining; and breathes with difficulty, and coughs and vomits a large amount of blood, and it is a serious condition, and the ancients have applied great ingenuity to it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And there are some who say that it is necessary to administer foods which swell the belly, to push the fracture outwards.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, lest hot abscesses develop there, if they have not already.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they are there, then treat them.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some of them say that one should place cupping glasses on the area, to draw strongly, and this seems reasonable; however, there is concern that the cupping glass may attract excess fluids to the area due to its weakened state.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some of them say that one should cover the area with wool soaked in hot oil, and place tents between the ribs to make the place even all around, then it should be treated with the treatment for pleurisy, with food and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear from the bone that pierces the tissue, and there is concern for the patient, it is necessary to cut over the location of the broken rib, and it is necessary to place an instrument underneath to protect the peritoneum; and then one must cut the bone, and pull it gently, and then sew the two edges of the wound, if it is large, and treat it with plasters, until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if hot abscesses develop, then apply cloths soaked in rose oil, and place them on the area; and meanwhile treat the area as appropriate for an abscess, and let him lie often on the side where he should, until he is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the fracture of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes a fracture occurs in the bones of the neck, and rarely does it bend; and also in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if he will recover or not, take note if you see his hands softened and swollen and dead, and he cannot move or extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, he does not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that he is mortally [injured] in several ways, and if he moves them and feels well when they are squeezed and pricked, know that the joint of the bone is safe, and that the patient will be cured, if treatment is applied.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if a similar thing happens to the spine of the back, and you want to know if he will be healed or not, take note if the feet are softened, and if the same things happen to them as to the hands, and on the back there is flatulence and involuntary defecation; and when he is turned on his stomach, there is involuntary defecation.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is turned on his back and he wants to sit up, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that he is mortally [injured]: so do not work on his treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if these symptoms do not occur, the matter is less serious.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that you see if there is a hot abscess, then put on the spine rose oil or oil of egg yolks, until it is soothed; then apply one of the strengthening and drying plasters, and bind it with a bandage, and tell the patient to rest; and do not sleep on the side where he feels the pain, until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is separated, it is necessary to cut to the heart of it; and remove the bone, then bring together the two edges of the wound, if it is large, with a suture, then treat it with an ointment that generates flesh, until it is healed; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "tail head", put in the thumb of your left hand, and align it with your other hand as best you can, then apply the plaster and splint on top, if you need it; then tighten it, and if there is a separated bone, cut into it, and remove it, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the hip bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It rarely happens that the hip bone is broken, and if it does happen, it is only a small break at the head; and it runs lengthwise, and slopes downwards, and the patient feels pain in the area, and a pricking sensation, and swelling where it is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand over it, until you are on the fracture; and know what the fracture is like and its shape; and if the fracture is only at the head, align this fracture so that it returns to its natural shape.
